RECONSTRUCT WHOLESALER ALLOCATION ==============\n\nprint(\"Reconstructing wholesaler allocation...\")\n\n# For each day, we have:\n# - Total supply of each product from producers\n# - Store orders (previous days' unfilled + new orders)\n# - The orders are filled first-come-first-served\n\n# We need to figure out the allocation of products to stores each day.\n# The total delivered to stores matches total received from producers.\n\n# For each day:\n# 1. Start with available inventory of each product (carried over from previous days)\n# 2. Add new producer deliveries\n# 3. Fill store orders in order of store sequence\n\n# Since total delivered = total received, the wholesaler is a pass-through\n# Let's track pending orders as a FIFO queue\n\n# Pending orders: list of (day_ordered, store, product_order_dict)\npending_orders = OrderedDict()  # (order_day, store) -> {product: qty}\n\n# Add all orders in order of day, then store sequence\nprint(\"  Building order queue...\")\norder_queue = []\nfor day in sorted(orders.keys()):\n    d, s = day\n    seq_info = store_receipts.get(d, {}).get(s, {})\n    seq = seq_info.get('seq', 100)\n    order_queue.append((d, seq, s, orders[day]))\n\norder_queue.sort(key=lambda x: (x[0], x[1]))\norder_index = 0  # current position in the queue\n\n# Track which orders have been fully/partially fulfilled\n# For each store-day order, track remaining qty per product\npending = OrderedDict()  # (day, store) -> {product: remaining_qty}\nfulfilled = {}  # (day, store) -> {product: allocated_qty}\n\n# Create pending orders\nfor d, seq, s, items in order_queue:\n    pending[(d, s)] = dict(items)\n    fulfilled[(d, s)] = {p: 0 for p in items}\n\n# Track inventory at wholesaler (per product, as a queue of (producer, qty))\n# Since wholesaler is pass-through, inventory is just what's available\nwholesaler_inventory = defaultdict(list)  # product -> [(producer, qty, delivery_day)]\n\n# Track product allocation per store per day\n# store -> day -> {product: qty, producer_info}\nstore_alloc = defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(list)))\n\nprint(\"  Simulating daily allocation...\")\nfor day in sorted(supply_by_day.keys()):\n    # Add new supply to wholesaler inventory\n    for prod, items in supply_by_day[day].items():\n        for supplier, qty, seq in items:\n            wholesaler_inventory[prod].append((supplier, qty, day))\n    \n    # Get stores served on this day, in sequence order\n    stores_today = store_receipts.get(day, {})\n    store_order = sorted(stores_today.keys(), key=lambda s: stores_today[s]['seq'])\n    \n    for store in store_order:\n        # Find the oldest pending order for this store\n        # Orders might have been placed earlier\n        # The store has a delivery receipt today, so some order is being fulfilled\n        order_key = None\n        for ok in list(pending.keys()):\n            if ok[1] == store and any(v > 0 for v in pending[ok].values()):\n                order_key = ok\n                # Check if this order has pending items\n                if sum(pending[ok].values()) > 0:\n                    break\n        \n        if order_key is None:\n            # No pending order for this store, check if there are orders placed today\n            if (day, store) in pending and sum(pending[(day, store)].values()) > 0:\n                order_key = (day, store)\n            else:\n                continue\n        \n        # Try to fulfill this order from wholesaler inventory\n        for prod in list(pending[order_key].keys()):\n            needed = pending[order_key][prod]\n            if needed <= 0:\n                continue\n            \n            # Take from wholesaler FIFO inventory\n            taken = 0\n            while taken < needed and len(wholesaler_inventory[prod]) > 0:\n                supplier, batch_qty, delivery_day = wholesaler_inventory[prod][0]\n                take = min(batch_qty, needed - taken)\n                if take > 0:\n                    store_alloc[store][day][prod].append((supplier, take, delivery_day))\n                    taken += take\n                    if take >= batch_qty:\n                        wholesaler_inventory[prod].pop(0)\n                    else:\n                        wholesaler_inventory[prod][0] = (supplier, batch_qty - take, delivery_day)\n            \n            # Update pending and fulfilled\n            pending[order_key][prod] = needed - taken\n            fulfilled[order_key][prod] = fulfilled[order_key].get(prod, 0) + taken\n\n# ============== 7. RECONSTRUCT STORE INVENTORY ==============\n\nprint(\"Reconstructing store inventory...\")\n\n# For each store-product, track FIFO inventory as batches from producers\nstore_inventory = defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(list))\n\n# Track store sales and when batches are consumed\n# For each store, the sales_log tells us how much was sold each day per product\n# We need to match sales to inventory batches\n\n# Let's build the timeline for each store-product\nstore_product_timeline = defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(list))\n\nfor store in sorted(set(s[0] for s in store_alloc.keys())):\n    for day in sorted(store_alloc[store].keys()):\n        for prod in store_alloc[store][day]:\n            for supplier, qty, del_day in store_alloc[store][day][prod]:\n                store_inventory[store][prod].append({\n                    'supplier': supplier,\n                    'qty': qty,\n                    'receive_day': day,\n                    'delivery_day': del_day,\n                    'remaining': qty\n                })\n\n# Simulate FIFO sales\n# For each store-product-day, we sell min(sold_qty, available_inventory)\n# Track which batches were used\n\n# Group sales log by store-product-day\nsales_by_sp = defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(int)))\nwith open(f'{DATA_DIR}/sales_log.csv') as fh:\n    reader = csv.DictReader(fh)\n    for row in reader:\n        day = int(row['Day'])\n        store = row['Store_ID']\n        prod = row['Product_ID']\n        sold = int(row['Sold_Quantity'])\n        if sold > 0:\n            sales_by_sp[store][prod][day] = sales_by_sp[store][prod].get(day, 0) + sold\n\n# Track which batches are sold and quality events\nbatch_consumed_days = defaultdict(list)  # (store, prod, supplier) -> list of days consumed\nconsumer_events = []  # track quality events\n\nprint(\"  Simulating FIFO sales and detecting quality events...\")\nfor store in sales_by_sp:\n    for prod in sales_by_sp[store]:\n        inv = store_inventory[store][prod]\n        if not inv:\n            continue\n        inv_idx = 0\n        for day in sorted(sales_by_sp[store][prod].keys()):\n            to_sell = sales_by_sp[store][prod][day]\n            while to_sell > 0 and inv_idx < len(inv):\n                batch = inv[inv_idx]\n                sell = min(batch['remaining'], to_sell)\n                if sell > 0:\n                    batch['remaining'] -= sell\n                    to_sell -= sell\n                    # Record that this batch was consumed on this day\n                    batch_consumed_days[(store, prod, batch['supplier'])].append(day)\n                if batch['remaining'] == 0:\n                    inv_idx += 1\n\n# ============== 8. DETECT QUALITY EVENTS FROM DEMAND PATTERNS ==============\n\nprint(\"Detecting quality events from demand patterns...\")\n\n# For each product, aggregate demand across all stores\n# The recovery pattern: 3 days at 20%, 4 days at 50%, 7 days at 80%, then back\n\n# Load aggregated daily demand per product\nproduct_daily = defaultdict(lambda: {'demand': 0, 'sold': 0})\nwith open(f'{DATA_DIR}/sales_log.csv') as fh:\n    reader = csv.DictReader(fh)\n    for row in reader:\n        day = int(row['Day'])\n        prod = row['Product_ID']\n        product_daily[day][prod] = product_daily[day].get(prod, {'demand': 0, 'sold': 0})\n        product_daily[day][prod]['demand'] += int(row['Reported_Demand'])\n        product_daily[day][prod]['sold'] += int(row['Sold_Quantity'])\n\n# Normalize demand by the number of consumers\n# Each consumer has a base demand of 2-3\n# Count consumers per day per product\nconsumer_counts = defaultdict(lambda: defaultdict(int))\nwith open(f'{DATA_DIR}/sales_log.csv') as fh:\n    reader = csv.DictReader(fh)\n    for row in reader:\n        day = int(row['Day'])\n        prod = row['Product_ID']\n        consumer_counts[day][prod] += 1\n\n# Per-product analysis: find demand drops that match the recovery pattern\n# The recovery signature: a sharp drop followed by gradual recovery over 14 days\n\n# For each product, look at average demand per consumer\nprint(\"  Computing demand per consumer by product...\")\nproducts = sorted(set(row['Product_ID'] for row in csv.DictReader(open(f'{DATA_DIR}/sales_log.csv'))))\nall_products = sorted(set(f'P_{i}' for i in range(1, 31)))\n\nproduct_baseline = {}\nproduct_quality_drops = defaultdict(list)\n\nfor prod in all_products:\n    daily_avg_demand = {}\n    for day in range(1, 366):\n        cnt = consumer_counts[day].get(prod, 0)\n        dem = product_daily[day].get(prod, {}).get('demand', 0)\n        if cnt > 0:\n            daily_avg_demand[day] = dem / cnt\n        else:\n            daily_avg_demand[day] = None\n    \n    # Estimate baseline demand per consumer (ignoring recovery effects)\n    # Use the 90th percentile of observed values as baseline\n    valid_vals = [v for v in daily_avg_demand.values() if v is not None]\n    if valid_vals:\n        # Baseline is the mode (most common value per consumer - should be 2 or 3)\n        from collections import Counter\n        val_counts = Counter(valid_vals)\n        baseline = val_counts.most_common(1)[0][0]\n        product_baseline[prod] = baseline\n    else:\n        product_baseline[prod] = 2.5\n\nprint(f\"  Product baselines: {dict(sorted(product_baseline.items()))}\")\n\n# Now detect recovery patterns\n# A recovery event starts when:\n# 1. A batch is consumed (sold)\n# 2. After that, demand drops below baseline\n# 3. The demand follows the 14-day recovery pattern\n\n# The recovery pattern reduces demand multiplier:\nrecovery_pattern = {1: 0.2, 2: 0.2, 3: 0.2, 4: 0.5, 5: 0.5, 6: 0.5, 7: 0.5,\n                    8: 0.8, 9: 0.8, 10: 0.8, 11: 0.8, 12: 0.8, 13: 0.8, 14: 0.8}\n\n# For each product, find periods where actual demand is below baseline\n# by an amount consistent with consumers in recovery\n\n# Approach: look at each day when inventory was sold\n# If after that day, demand drops in a pattern consistent with recovery,\n# then the batch sold on that day was bad\n\nconfirmed_offenders = defaultdict(set)  # product -> set of producers\n\n# For each product and each store, track demand to find recovery events\nprint(\"  Scanning for quality events per store-product...\")\nfor store in sorted(sales_by_sp.keys()):\n    for prod in sorted(sales_by_sp[store].keys()):\n        # Get daily demand and sales data for this store-product\n        sp_data = {}\n        with open(f'{DATA_DIR}/sales_log.csv') as fh:\n            reader = csv.DictReader(fh)\n            for row in reader:\n                if row['Store_ID'] == store and row['Product_ID'] == prod:\n                    day = int(row['Day'])\n                    if day not in sp_data:\n                        sp_data[day] = {'demand': 0, 'sold': 0}\n                    sp_data[day]['demand'] += int(row['Reported_Demand'])\n                    sp_data[day]['sold'] += int(row['Sold_Quantity'])\n        \n        if not sp_data:\n            continue\n        \n        # Get consumers per day\n        sp_consumers = {}\n        with open(f'{DATA_DIR}/sales_log.csv') as fh:\n            reader = csv.DictReader(fh)\n            for row in reader:\n                if row['Store_ID'] == store and row['Product_ID'] == prod:\n                    day = int(row['Day'])\n                    if day not in sp_consumers:\n                        sp_consumers[day] = 0\n                    sp_consumers[day] += 1\n        \n        if not sp_consumers:\n            continue\n        \n        avg_demand_per_consumer = product_baseline.get(prod, 2.5)\n        \n        # Compute expected demand without quality effects\n        # We need to separate calendar effects and quality effects\n        # Calendar effects are product-specific and shared across stores\n        \n        # For simplicity, use a rolling median as baseline\n        days_list = sorted(sp_data.keys())\n        baseline_demand = {}\n        for i, d in enumerate(days_list):\n            # Use median of surrounding days as baseline\n            surrounding = []\n            for j in range(max(0, i-7), min(len(days_list), i+8)):\n                sd = days_list[j]\n                surrounding.append(sp_data[sd]['demand'] / max(sp_consumers[sd], 1))\n            surrounding.sort()\n            baseline_demand[d] = surrounding[len(surrounding)//2] * sp_consumers.get(d, 1)\n        \n        # Find demand drops that persist\n        # Check each day that had sales (potential bad batch day)\n        for d in days_list:\n            sold = sp_data[d]['sold']\n            if sold <= 0:\n                continue\n            \n            # Check if this batch might have been bad\n            # After day d, demand should drop for 14 days\n            expected_demand = [baseline_demand.get(d + offset, 0) for offset in range(1, 15)]\n            actual_demand = [sp_data.get(d + offset, {}).get('demand', 0) for offset in range(1, 15)]\n            \n            if len([a for a in actual_demand if a > 0]) < 5:\n                continue  # Not enough data\n            \n            # Check if the actual demand follows the recovery pattern\n            # For each day in recovery, expected demand = baseline * recovery_multiplier\n            pattern_demand = []\n            for offset in range(1, 15):\n                mult = recovery_pattern[offset]\n                exp = baseline_demand.get(d + offset, 0) * mult\n                pattern_demand.append(exp)\n            \n            # Calculate how well the actual follows the pattern\n            deviations = []\n            for offset in range(1, 15):\n                act = actual_demand[offset - 1]\n                pat = pattern_demand[offset - 1]\n                base = baseline_demand.get(d + offset, 1)\n                if base > 0:\n                    deviations.append(abs(act - pat) / base)\n            \n            if deviations:\n                avg_dev = sum(deviations) / len(deviations)\n                # It should be the oldest pending order for that store.\n# If store S placed orders on days 1, 4, 7 and gets deliveries on days 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7...\n# The delivery on day 1 fulfills the oldest unfilled order (from day 1).\n# Once day 1's order is fully fulfilled, day 4's order is next.\n\n# Strategy: maintain for each store a queue of pending orders\n# For each day, process stores in sequence order\n# For each store, find the oldest pending order with unfilled items\n# Fill it from available inventory\n\n# Pending orders: store -> [(day_ordered, {product: qty})]\nstore_pending = defaultdict(list)\nfor (d, s), items in sorted(orders.items(), key=lambda x: x[0]):\n    store_pending[s].append([d, dict(items)])\n\n# Fulfilled amounts: (day_ordered, store, product) -> qty\nfulfilled_amounts = defaultdict(int)\n\n# Wholesaler inventory: product -> [(supplier, qty, delivery_day)]\nwh_inv = defaultdict(list)\n\n# Track store allocations: (store, day) -> [(product, supplier, qty, delivery_day)]\nstore_allocations = defaultdict(list)\n\n# Process day by day\nfor day in sorted(supply_by_day.keys()):\n    # Followed by four days of moderately lower demand (days 4-7)\n3. Followed by seven days of slightly lower demand (days 8-14)\n4. Instead of trying to detect recovery patterns in the demand data, let me work backward from the LOST SALES data.\n\nThe problem says: \"Low-quality deliveries can temporarily reduce future sales because disappointed consumers may stop buying a product for some time.\"\n\nSo the impact of quality is on FUTURE DEMAND (which shows up as Lost_Sales if there IS inventory but the demand is satisfied, or just lower demand otherwise).\n\nWait, actually, the impact is on future DEMAND, which is the Reported_Demand. If a consumer is in recovery, their Reported_Demand is lower. Then the store tries to satisfy this lower demand from inventory.\n\nSo the effect is:\n1. Bad batch consumed on day D\n2. Starting day D+1, the affected consumers report lower demand\n3. This lower demand persists for 14 days\n\nThe net effect on the store is: lower Reported_Demand for 14 days.\n\nNow, the store's inventory determines whether this lower demand translates to sales or not. If the store has enough inventory, the sales also drop. If the store doesn't have inventory, the lost_sales also drop (since demand is lower).\n\nEither way, the lower Reported_Demand is the key signal.\n\nBut the problem is that the signal is small relative to noise.\n\nLet me try a completely different approach. Instead of individual detection, let me use an AGGREGATE approach:\n\nFor each product and each producer, compute the AVERAGE demand change after their batches are consumed.\n\nIf a producer's batches are bad, then after consumption, the demand should drop (on average) for 14 days. If the batches are good, there should be no systematic change.\n\nThis is like an event study in finance. Let me compute:\n- For each producer-product pair, find all days when their batch was consumed\n- For each such day, compute the demand change relative to baseline for the next 14 days\n- Average across all events\n- If the average shows the recovery pattern, that producer is confirmed\n\nThis should work because averaging across many events reduces noise.","time":{"start":1781021407812,"end":1781021417609}}}
